RIG VEDA - MODERN ENGLISH & HINGLISH REWRITE
==================================================

==================================================
RIG-VEDA, BOOK 1
==================================================

--------------------------------------------------
HYMN I. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01001.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 I praise Agni, the chosen Priest, God, minister of sacrifice,
The hotar, richest in wealth.
2 Agni is worthy to be praised by living as by ancient seers.
He will bring the Gods hither.
3 Through Agni, man obtains wealth, indeed, growing more each day,
Most rich in heroes, glorious.
4 Agni, the perfect sacrifice that you encompass,
Verily goes to the Gods.
5 May Agni, wise-minded Priest, truthful, most gloriously great,
The God, come hither with the Gods.
6 Whatever blessing, Agni, you grant to your worshipper,
That, Aṅgiras, is indeed your truth.
7 To you, dispeller of the night, O Agni, day by day with prayer,
Bringing you reverence, we come.
8 Ruler of sacrifices, guardian of Eternal Law, radiant One,
Increasing in your own abode.
9 Be to us easy of approach, even as a father to his son:
Agni, be with us for our well-being.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN II. Vāyu.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01002.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 BEAUTIFUL Vāyu, come, for you these Soma drops have been prepared:
Drink of them, listen to our call.
2 Knowing the days, with Soma juice poured forth, the singers glorify
You, Vāyu, with their hymns of praise.
3 Vāyu, your penetrating stream goes forth to the worshipper,
Far-reaching for the Soma draught.
4 These, Indra-Vāyu, have been shed; come for our offered dainties’ sake:
The drops are yearning for you both.
5 Well do you mark libations, Vāyu and Indra, rich in spoil!
So come swiftly hitherward.
6 Vāyu and Indra, come to what the Soma-presser has prepared:
Soon, Heroes, thus I make my prayer.
7 Mitra, of holy strength, I call, and foe-destroying Varuṇa,
Who make the oil-fed rite complete.
8 Mitra and Varuṇa, through Law, lovers and cherishers of Law,
Have you obtained your might power?
9 Our Sages, Mitra-Varuṇa, wide dominion, strong by birth,
Vouchsafe us strength that works well.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN III. Aśvins
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01003.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O Aśvins, rich in treasures, lords of brilliance, with nimble hands,
 Accept the sacrificial offerings.

2 O Aśvins, rich in wonderful deeds, you heroes worthy of praise,
 Accept our songs with great thoughts.

3 Nāsatyas, wonder-workers, your libations with clippings of grass:
 Come, whose paths are red with fire.

4 O Indra, brightly splendid, come, these libations long for you,
 Thus purified by skilled hands.

5 Urged by the holy singer, carried by song, come, Indra, to the prayers,
 Of the libation-pouring priest.

6 Approach, O Indra, hastening to the prayers, Lord of Bay Horses,
 In our libation take delight.

7 You Viśvedevas, who protect, reward, and cherish men, approach
 Your worshipper’s drink-offering.

8 You Viśvedevas, swift at work, come quickly to the draught,
 Like milch kine to their stalls.

9 The Viśvedevas, changing shape like serpents, fearless, without deceit,
 Carriers, accept the sacred draught.

10 Wealthy in spoils, enriched with hymns, may bright Sarasvatī desire,
 With eager love, our sacrifice.

11 Inciter of all pleasant songs, inspirer of all gracious thoughts,
 Sarasvatī accept our rites.

12 Sarasvatī, the mighty river—she with her light illuminates,
 She brightens every pious thought.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN IV. Indra
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01004.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 As a good cow to the one who milks it, we call the doer of good deeds,
To our assistance every day.
2 Come to our libations, drink of Soma; Soma-drinker you are!
The wealthy One gives cows as rapture.
3 May we know your innermost kindness:
Do not neglect us, come hither.
4 Go to the wise, undefeated One, ask Indra, skilled in song,
Who is better than your friends.
5 Whether those who mock us say, "Go to another place,"
You who serve Indra and no one else;
6 Or whether, God of wonderful deeds, all our true people call us blessed,
Still may we dwell in Indra’s care.
7 Bring the swift One speed, cheering man, the grace of sacrifice,
That to the Friend gives wings and joy.
8 You, Śatakratu, drank this and were the Vṛtras' slayer; you
Help the warrior in battle.
9 We strengthen, Śatakratu, you, the powerful in battle,
That, Indra, we may win wealth.
10 To him the mighty stream of wealth, dear friend of him who pours the juice,
Yes, to this Indra sing your song.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN V. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01005.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Come here and sit down, sing a hymn to Indra, dear friends,
2 To him, the richest of the rich, the lord of treasures excellent,
Indra, with Soma juice poured out.
3 May he stand by us in our need and be abundant for our wealth,
May he come near us with his might.
4 Whose pair of tawny horses, yoked in battle, foes dare not challenge:
To him, to Indra, sing your song.
5 Come close to the Soma drinker, for his enjoyment, these pure drops,
The Somas mixed with curds.
6 You, grown to perfect strength, were born to drink the Soma juice,
Strong Indra, for preeminence.
7 O Indra, lover of the song, may these quick Somas enter you:
May they bring bliss to you, Sage.
8 Our praises have strengthened you, O Śatakratu, and our lauds
So strengthen you the songs we sing.
9 Indra, whose succor never fails, accept these offerings tenfold,
Wherein all manly powers abide.
10 O Indra, you who love song, let no man harm our bodies, keep
Slaughter far from us, for you can.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN VI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01006.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 They stand around him as he moves, harnessing the bright, ruddy Horse
 The stars shine in the sky.
 2 On both sides they yoke the two fine horses dear to him,
 Bold, tawny, bearing the Chief.
 3 You, creating light where there was none, and form, O men: where form wasn't,
 Were born with the Dawn.
 4 Afterwards, as usual, they cast off the state of unformed infants,
 Taking sacrificial names.
 5 You, Indra, with the Storm-Gods, the ones breaking down what stands firm,
 Found the cattle even in the cave.
 6 Worshiping as they please, singers praise him who finds wealth,
 The renowned far and mighty One.
 7 May you truly be seen coming by fearless Indra's side:
 Both joyful, equal in your radiance.
 8 With Indra's beloved hosts, blameless and hastening to heaven,
 The sacrificer cries aloud.
 9 Come from this place, O Wanderer, or downward from the light of heaven:
 Our praises all yearn for this.
 10 Indra, we seek your help, from here, from heaven above the earth,
 Or from the vast firmament.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN VII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01007.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Indra, the singers sing high praise, Indra, the reciters chant their songs,
Indra, the choirs have glorified.
2 Indra has always close by his two swift horses and chariot yoked,
Indra, golden, armed with thunder.
3 Indra raises the Sun high in the sky so he can see far off,
He bursts mountains to let the cattle pass.
4 Help us, O Indra, in battles, in battles where many prizes are won,
With awesome aid, O awesome One.
5 In great battles we invoke Indra, Indra in small fights too,
The friend who turns his arrow at foes.
6 Open, our brave Hero, you who are ever generous up there,
For us, you unyielding one.
7 Higher still, with each line I sing, Indra's praises rise with thunder,
I find no words worthy of him.
8 As a bull drives the herd, he leads the people with his might,
The Ruler, unstoppable:
9 Indra who rules with single rule over men, wealth, and the five races,
Of those who live on Earth.
10 For your sake, from all sides we call Indra away from others,
Ours, and none others', may he be.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN VIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01008.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Indra, grant us wealth that brings joy, the invincible wealth of the victorious,
Most excellent, to be our aid;
2 By which we can repel our enemies hand-to-hand,
With your help on chariots we shall fight.
3 With you, the thunder-armed Indra, may we lift the bolt,
And conquer all our foes in battle.
4 With you, O Indra, as ally with dart-wielding heroes,
May we conquer our foes in battle.
5 Great is Indra, indeed supreme; may his might be vast,
As wide as heaven, extending far.
6 It aids those who come as heroes to the fight,
Or singers with pure thoughts.
7 His belly, drinking deep Soma, swells like an ocean,
Like wide streams from the sky.
8 His excellence, great and strong, rich in cattle,
Like a ripe branch to the worshipper.
9 Indeed, your mighty powers, Indra, are saving helps,
For me, a worshipper like you.
10 His lovely gifts are many; let lauds and praises be to Indra,
That he may drink the Soma juice.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN IX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01009.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Come, Indra, and be delighted with the Soma juice at all feasts,
Protector, mighty in your strength.
2 Pour forth the Soma juice to Indra, this joy-bringing juice to him,
The joy-bringing, all-powerful God.
3 You Lord of all men, fair-skinned, rejoice in the joyous hymns,
Present at these drink-offerings.
4 Songs have risen to you, Indra, the strong, the guardian Lord,
And they have risen unsatisfied.
5 Send us manifold abundance, O Indra, worthy of our wish,
For only you possess supreme power.
6 Indra, stir up in us a desire for wealth, glorious and splendid,
Most splendid One.
7 Give, Indra, wide and lofty fame, rich in cattle and strength,
Lasting our lives, never failing.
8 Grant us high fame, O Indra, riches that bring thousands, these
Fruits of the earth carried home in wagons.
9 Praising with songs the worthy one who comes to our aid, we call
Indra, the Wealth-Lord of treasure.
10 Sing aloud a strengthening hymn to Indra, the Lord of wealth,
Who dwells by each libation, the pious man.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN X. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01010.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 The chanters praise you, those who speak the word of honor.
 Priests have raised you high, O Śatakratu, like a pole.
 2 As he climbs from ridge to ridge and sees the hard work,
 Indra watches this wish of his, and the Rain comes with his troop.
 3 Harness your strong horses, long-haired, whose bodies fill the girths,
 And, Indra, Soma-drinker, come to listen to our songs.
 4 Come here, answer our song, sing in approval, shout loud.
 Good Indra, make our prayer successful, and prosper this sacrifice.
 5 To Indra must be said a laud, to strengthen him who freely gives,
 That Śakra may take pleasure in our friendship and drink-offerings.
 6 Him, him we seek for friendship, him for riches and heroic might.
 For Indra, he is Śakra, he will aid us with his wealth.
 7 It's easy to turn and drive away, Indra, the spoils you give.
 Open the stable of the kine, and give us wealth, Thunder-armed Indra.
 8 The heaven and earth cannot contain you, together, in your fury.
 Win us the waters of the sky, and send us many cows.
 9 Hear, you whose ears are quick, my call; take my songs readily.
 O Indra, let this laud of mine come closer than your friend.
 10 We know you are the mightiest, in battles hearing our cries.
 Most mighty, we invoke the aid that brings a thousand gifts.
 11 O Indra, Son of Kuśika, drink our libation with joy.
 Extend our life anew, and make the seer win a thousand gifts.
 12 Lover of song, may these songs surround you everywhere:
 Strengthening you with lengthened life, may they be dear delights to you.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01011.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 All sacred songs praise Indra, expansive like the ocean,
 The greatest warrior, borne on chariots, the Lord, the very Lord of might.
 2 Strong in your friendship, Indra, Lord of power and might, we have no fear.
 We glorify you with praises, the unconquered conqueror.
 3 From olden times, Indra's gifts, his saving aids, never fail,
 When he grants the boon of wealth in cattle to the singers.
 4 You crushed fortresses, the young and wise, of immeasurable strength,
 Supporter of every sacred rite, Indra, the Thunderer, much-praised.
 5 Lord of thunder, you burst the cave of Vala rich in cows.
 The gods came to your side, free from fear, aiding you,
 6 I, Hero, through your bounties have come to you, addressing you.
 Song-lover, here the singers stand and testify to you.
 7 Wily Śuṣṇa, Indra! You overcame with your marvelous powers.
 The wise saw this deed of yours; now go beyond their praise.
 8 Our songs of praise have glorified Indra, ruler by his might,
 Whose precious gifts in thousands come, indeed, even more abundantly.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XII. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01012.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 We summon Agni, the messenger, the herald, master of all wealth,
Well versed in this ritual offering.
2 They call upon Agni, Agni, Lord of the House,
Oblation-carrier, dear to us.
3 Bring the gods here, Agni, born for him who spreads the sacred grass:
You are our herald, worthy of praise.
4 Awaken the willing gods, for you, Agni, perform the embassy:
Sit on the sacred grass with gods.
5 Agni, radiant one, to whom the holy oil is poured, burn up
Our enemies, protected by fiends.
6 By Agni, Agni, inflamed, Lord of the House, wise, young, who bears
The gift: the ladle is his mouth.
7 Pray for Agni in the sacrifice, the Sage whose ways are always true,
The God who drives away sorrow.
8 God, Agni, be his strong defense, lord of sacrificial gifts,
Who worships you, the messenger.
9 May he, with sacred offering, call Agni to the gods' feast,
Purifier, grant him favor.
10 As Agni, Purifier, bright, bring prosperity to us,
And food, with heroes for our sons.
11 So praised by our newest hymn of praise, bring opulence to us,
And sustenance, for our sons.
12 O Agni, by your radiant flame, by all the gods' invocations,
Show pleasure in this praise of ours.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XIII. Agni
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01013.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 AGNI, well-kindled, bring the Devas for him who offers sacred offerings.
Worship them, Purifier, Priest.
2 Son of Thyself, present, O Sage, our sacrifice to the Devas today.
Sweet to the taste, that they may feast.
3 Dear Narāśaṁsa, sweet-tongued, the giver of oblations, I invoke
To this our sacrifice.
4 Agni, on your easy chariot, glorified, bring the Devas here:
Manu appointed you as Priest.
5 Scatter, O wise ones, the sacred grass dripping with oil,
Where the Immortals are seen.
6 Open be the Divine Doors, unceasing, that aid the ritual,
For this sacrifice today and now.
7 I call the lovely Night and Dawn to sit on the holy grass
At this solemn sacrifice.
8 I invite the two Invokers, the wise, sweet-tongued, divine,
To celebrate this sacrifice.
9 Iḷā, Sarasvatī, Mahī, three Goddesses who bring joy,
Be seated, peaceful, on the grass.
10 Tvaṣṭar I call, the firstborn, the one who can take any form:
May he be ours and ours alone.
11 God, Sovereign of the Wood, present this offering to the Devas,
And make the giver famous.
12 With Svāhā, pay the sacrifice to Indra in the house of the offerer:
There I call the Deities.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XIV. Viśvedevas.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01014.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 To drink the Soma, Agni, come, to our service and our songs.
With all these gods; and worship them.
2 The Kaṇvas have invoked thee; they, O singer, sing thee songs of praise
Agni, come hither with the gods;
3 Indra, Vāyu, Brihaspathi, Mitra, Agni, Pūṣan, Bhaga,
Adityas, and the Maruts, too.
4 For you these juices are poured forth that cheer and invigorate,
The mead resting in the cup.
5 The sons of Kaṇva seek your aid, having strewn the grass,
With offerings and all things prepared.
6 May swift steeds that bear you, yoked in thought and dripping holy oil,
Bring the gods to the Soma draught.
7 Adored, the lawgivers, unite them, Agni, with your wives:
Make them drink mead, O tongue of light.
8 Let them, O Agni, who deserve worship and praise drink with your tongue
The mead in solemn sacrifice.
9 Away, from the Sun’s realm of light, the wise invoking priest shall bring
All gods awoke with the dawn.
10 With all the gods, with Indra, with Vāyu, and Mitra’s splendor, drink,
Agni, the pleasant Soma juice.
11 Ordained by Manu as our priest, you sit at each rite:
Hallow this our sacrifice.
12 Harness the red mares to your chariot, the bay, O God, the fiery ones:
With those bring hitherward the gods.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XV. Ṛtu.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01015.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O Indra, drink the Soma juice with Ṛtu; may the cheering drops
 Sink deep within, which settle there.
2 Drink from the Purifier's cup, Maruts, with Ṛtu; sanctify
 The rite, for ye give precious gifts.
3 O Neṣṭar, with thy Dame accept our sacrifice; with Ṛtu drink,
 For thou art he who giveth wealth.
4 Bring the Gods, Agni; place them in the three appointed places:
 Surround them, and with Ṛtu drink.
5 Drink Soma after the Ṛtus, from the Brāhmaṇa's bounty: undissolved,
 O Indra, is thy friendship's bond.
6 Mitra, Varuṇa, whose ways are firm— a Power that none deceives—
 With Ṛtu ye have reached the rite.
7 The Soma-pressers, fain for wealth, praise the Wealth-giver in the rite,
 In sacrifices praise the God.
8 May the Wealth-giver grant to us riches that shall be far renowned.
 These things we gain, among the Gods.
9 He with the Ṛtu fain would drink, Wealth-giver, from the Neṣṭar's bowl.
 Haste, give your offering, and depart.
10 As we this fourth time, Wealth-giver, honour thee with the Ṛtus, be
 A Giver bountiful to us.
11 Drink ye the meath, O Aśvins bright with flames, whose acts are pure, who with
 Ṛtus accept the sacrifice.
12 With Ṛtu, through the house-fire, thou, kind Giver, guidest sacrifice:
 Worship the Gods for the pious man.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XVI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01016.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Let your swift horses bring you, the Strong One, here to drink the Soma juice—
Those, Indra, who shine as bright as suns.
2 Here are the grains drenched in oil; let the swift horses bring
Indra in his best chariot.
3 We call to you, Indra, at dawn, in the ritual, Indra,
To drink the Soma juice.
4 Come here, with your long-haired horses, O Indra, to the drink we offer
We call you when the juice is shed.
5 Come to this song of ours, Indra, to the libation we pour for you
Drink it like a thirsty stag.
6 Here are the drops of Soma juice extracted on sacred grass: drink them,
Indra, to grow mighty.
7 Welcome to you be this hymn of ours, reaching your heart, most excellent:
Then drink the Soma juice.
8 To every pressed juice, Indra, the slayer of Vṛtra, comes
To drink the Soma for joy.
9 May all our wishes be fulfilled, Indra, with horses and cattle,
With pure thoughts we sing your praise.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XVII. Indra-Varuṇa
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01017.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 I SEEK the aid of the Imperial Lords, Indra and Varuṇa; may they
 Both favor one of us like me.
2 You are protectors of men, always ready to help at the call
 Of any singer like myself.
3 May you, according to your will, O Indra and Varuṇa, be rich:
 We want you close by us.
4 May we share your powers, your kindness,
 That gives strength generously.
5 Indra and Varuṇa, among those who give much, worthy of praise,
 Are Powers deserving high praise.
6 With your protection, may we gain great wealth, and pile it up
 So plentifully that there's more than enough.
7 O Indra and Varuṇa, I call for wealth in all its forms:
 Keep us always victorious.
8 O Indra and Varuṇa, through our songs that seek to win you to us,
 Give us your immediate help.
9 O Indra and Varuṇa, let my fair praise reach you,
 A joint honor that you make great.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XVIII. Brahmaṇaspati.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01018.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O BRAHMANASPATHI, make Kakṣīvān Auśija glorious,
Even the rich one, healer of diseases, giver of wealth, one who increases stores,
The prompt one, may he be with us still.

2 Let not the foe’s curse, let not a mortal’s assault fall upon us;
Preserve us, BRAHMANASPATHI.

3 May Indra, BRAHMANASPATHI, and Soma graciously inspire the mortal hero,
Ne’er is the mortal hero harmed by them.

4 Do, thou, O BRAHMANASPATHI, and Indra, Soma, Dakṣiṇā,
Preserve that mortal from distress.

5 To the Assembly’s wondrous Lord, to Indra’s lovely friend who gives
Wisdom, have I drawn near in prayer.

6 He without whom no sacrifice, even of the wise man, prospers;
Stirring the sequence of thoughts.

7 He makes the offering prosper, he promotes the course of sacrifice:
Our praise voice goes to the gods.

8 I have seen Narāśaṁsa, him most resolute, most widely renowned,
As if the household priest of heaven.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XIX. Agni, Maruts.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01019.htm
--------------------------------------------------
To this fair sacrifice and drink the milky draught, you are called:
O Agni, with the Maruts come.

No mortal man, no God surpasses your mental might, O Mighty One:
O Agni, with the Maruts come.

All gods without deceit, who know the great expanse of mid-air:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

The terrible ones who sing their song, not to be vanquished by might:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

Brilliant, awesome in form, mighty, devourers of their enemies:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

Those who sit as Deities in heaven, above the sky's luminous dome:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

Those who scatter clouds across the sky, over the billowing sea:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

Those who spread their bright beams over the ocean in their might:
O Agni, with those Maruts come.

For you, to be your first draught, I pour the Soma-mixed mead:
O Agni, with the Maruts come.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XX. Ṛbhus.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01020.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 For the celestial race, this song of praise that showers wealth generously,
Was crafted by singers with their lips.

2 Those who, with their minds, created horses harnessed by a word,
Attained by deeds to sacrifice.

3 They fashioned a swift chariot for the two Nāsatyas, moving everywhere,
And made a nectar-giving cow.

4 The Rbhus, with potent prayers, honest and hardworking, restored
Their Father and Mother to youth.

5 Together came your cheering drops, surrounded by Indra and Maruts,
With the Ādityas and the Kings.

6 Newly wrought by God Tvaṣṭar’s hand, four ladles did you make—
7 Grant us wealth, to him who pours three times seven libations, indeed,
Give wealth, pleased with our praises.

8 As devout priests they held, through pious acts they earned a share,
In sacrifice with the gods.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XXI. Indra-Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01021.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Invoke we, Indra and Agni, with joy for their hymnal song:
Both are Soma-drinkers, dear to us.
2 Pray ye, O men, and sing high praise to Indra and Agni in holy rites:
Sing praises to them in sacred songs.
3 We invite Indra and Agni, Soma-drinkers, for their renown,
To the Soma draught, to Mitra's fame.
4 Powerful gods, bid them come to this libation ready here:
Indra and Agni, come to us.
5 Indra and Agni, mighty lords of our assembly, vanquish the demons:
May barren ones never devour.
6 Guard ye, through this truth, in sight of wide view,
Indra and Agni, grant us bliss.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XXII. Aśvins and Others
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01022.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Awaken the Aśvins, who harness their chariot at dawn: may they
Approach to sip this Soma juice.

2 We invoke the Aśvins Two, the noble-borne gods in a fine chariot, the best
Charioteers who reach the heavens.

3 With honey-dipped reins you drive, Aśvins, and sprinkle the sacrifice
With your pleasant whips.

4 As you journey in your chariot, not far, O Aśvins, is the home
Of him who offers Soma juice.

5 For my protection, I invoke the golden-armed Savitar.
He knows, as a god, the place.

6 That he may send us aid, praise the Waters’ Offspring Savitar:
We seek his holy ways.

7 We call upon him, distributor of wondrous bounty and wealth,
On Savitar who sees men.

8 Come here, friends, and sit down, Savitar, to be praised by us,
Giving good gifts, it’s beautiful.

9 May Agni bring to us the willing spouses of the gods,
And Tvaṣṭar, to the Soma draught.

10 Most youthful Agni, bring their spouses, Hotrā, Bhāratī,
Varūtrī, Dhiṣaṇā, for aid.

11 Spouses of heroes, goddesses, with full wings may they come to us
With great protection and aid.

12 Indrāṇī, Varuṇānī, and Agnāyī, I invite you here,
For our well-being, to drink the Soma juice.

13 May Heaven and Earth, the mighty pair, drench our sacrifice
And feed us full with nourishment.

14 Their waters rich with fat, there in the Gandharva’s steadfast place,
The singers taste through sacred songs.

15 Thornless be thou, O Earth, spread wide before us for a dwelling-place:
Vouchsafe us shelter broad and sure.

16 The gods be gracious to us from the place where Vishnu strides
Through the seven earth regions!

17 Through all this world, Vishnu strides; thrice his foot he plants, and all
Is gathered in his step’s dust.

18 Vishnu, the guardian, whom none deceives, made three steps; henceforth
Establishing his high decrees.

19 Look on Vishnu’s works, by which the friend of Indra, closely


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XXIII. Vāyu and Others.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01023.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1. Strong are the Somas; come nigh, these juices mixed with milk;
Drink, Vāyu, the offered draughts.

2. Both Deities who touch the sky, Indra and Vāyu, we invoke
To drink of this our Soma juice.

3. Singers seek your aid, invoke Indra and Vāyu, swift as thought,
The thousand-eyed, the Lords of thought.

4. Mitra and Varuṇa, renowned as Gods of sacred might,
We call to drink the Soma juice.

5. Those who uphold the Law, Lords of the shining light of Law,
Mitra I call, and Varuṇa.

6. Let Varuṇa be our chief defense, let Mitra guard us with all aid,
Both make us rich exceedingly.

7. Indra, by Maruts surrounded, we call to drink the Soma juice;
May he fill himself with his troop.

8. Gods, Marut hosts led by Indra, distributors of Pūṣan’s gifts,
Listen to all my cry.

9. With Indra as ally, strike down Vṛtra, bounteous Gods,
Let not the wicked master us.

10. We call the Universal Gods, and Maruts to the Soma draught,
For strong are Pṛśni’s sons.

11. Comes the Maruts’ thundering voice, like conquerors’ when you go
Forward to victory, O Men.

12. Born of the laughing lightning, may the Maruts guard us everywhere,
May they be gracious to us.

13. Like some lost animal, drive to us, bright Pūṣan, him who bears up heaven,
Resting on many-coloured grass.

14. Pūṣan the Bright has found the King, concealed and hidden in a cave,
Who rests on grass of many hues.

15. And may he, through these drops, bring the six tightly bound,
As one who ploughs with steers brings corn.

16. Along their paths the Mothers go, Sisters of priestly ministrants,
Mingling their sweetness with the milk.

17. May Waters gathered near the Sun, and those with the Sun joined,
Speed forth this sacrifice of ours.

18. I call the Waters, Goddesses, wherein our cattle quench their thirst;
Oblations to the Streams be given.

19. Amrit in the Waters, in the Waters healing balm,

HYMN XXIV. Varuṇa and Others.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01024.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Who now is he, what deity among the Immortals, whose auspicious name can we recall?
 Who will restore us to mighty Aditi so that I may behold my Father and Mother?

2 Agni, the God, the first among the Immortals—let us recall his auspicious name.
 He will restore us to mighty Aditi so that I may behold my Father and Mother.

3 To you, O Savitar, Lord of precious things, who helps us continually,
 For our share we come—
4 Wealth, highly praised before reproach has touched it, laid free from hate,
 In your hands, safe and sound.

5 May your protection bring us to even the height of prosperity
 That Bhaga has bestowed upon us.

6 No birds that soar through the air have reached your high domain, your might, or your spirit;
 Nor have the waters that flow forever, nor the hills, which curb the wind’s wild fury.

7 Varuṇa, King, of pure might, upholds the Tree’s trunk in the void.
 Its rays, whose roots are high, descend. May they sink deep within us and be concealed.

8 King Varuṇa has made a broad path, a path for the Sun to traverse.
 Where no way was made, he set his steps, warning off whatever afflicts the spirit.

9 A hundred balms are yours, O King, a thousand; also deep and wide-reaching are your favors.
 Drive far away destruction, far from us, and remove even the sin we’ve committed.

10 By day, where do the stars that shine at night depart, set high above us?
 Varuṇa’s holy laws remain unchanged, and the Moon moves on in splendor through the night.

11 I pray to you with my offering, my worshipper asks for this.
 Varuṇa, stay here and be not angry; take not our life, O Wide-Ruler.

12 Every night and every day, they tell me this, and my own thoughts repeat it.
 May he who is bound by Śunaḥśepa, may he Sovrant Varuṇa release us.

13 Bound by three pillars, Śunaḥśepa made his plea to the Ādityas.
 May Sovrant Varuṇa deliver him, wise and untricked, loosen the bonds that bind him.

14 With offerings, sacrifices, Varuṇa, we deprecate your anger:
 Wise Asura, King of

HYMN XXV. Varuṇa.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01025.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 WHATEVER law of you, O God, O Varuṇa, as we are men,
 Day after day we break.
2 Give us not as a prey to death, to be destroyed by you in wrath,
 To your fierce anger when displeased.
3 To gain your mercy, Varuṇa, with hymns we bind your heart, as binds
 The charioteer his tethered horse.
4 They flee from me dispirited, bent only on obtaining wealth,
 As to their nests the birds of air.
5 When shall we bring, to be appeased, the Hero, Lord of warrior might,
 Him, the far-seeing Varuṇa?
6 This, this with joy they both accept in common: never do they fail
 The ever-faithful worshipper.
7 He knows the path of birds that fly through heaven, and, Sovran of the sea,
 He knows the ships that are thereon.
8 True to his holy law, he knows the twelve moons with their progeny:
 He knows the moon of later birth.
9 He knows the pathway of the wind, the spreading, high, and mighty wind:
 He knows the Gods who dwell above.
10 Varuṇa, true to holy law, sits down among his people; he,
 Most wise, sits there to govern all.
11 From thence perceiving he beholds all wondrous things, both what hath been,
 And what hereafter will be done.
12 May that Āditya, very wise, make fair paths for us all our days:
 May he prolong our lives for us.
13 Varuṇa, wearing golden mail, hath clad him in a shining robe.
 His spies are seated found about.
14 The God whom enemies threaten not, nor those who tyrannize o’er men,
 Nor those whose minds are bent on wrong.
15 He who gives glory to mankind, not glory that is incomplete,
 To our own bodies giving it.
16 Yearning for the wide-seeing One, my thoughts move onward unto him,
 As kine unto their pastures move.
17 Once more together let us speak, because my meath is brought: priest-like
 Thou eatest what is dear to thee.
18 Now saw I him whom all may see, I saw his car above the earth:
 He hath accepted these my songs.
19 Varuṇa, hear this call of mine: be gracious unto us this day
 Long

HYMN XXVI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01026.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O Agni worthy of offering, Lord of prosperous powers, clothe yourself,
 And perform this sacrifice for us.

2 Sit always chosen, as our priest, the youngest, through our hymns,
 O Agni, through our heavenly word.
3 Here, a father for his son, kin for kin, and friend for his friend,
 Offer sacrifices as men do.
4 Here may the destroyers of foes sit, Varuṇa, Mitra, Aryaman,
 Like men, on our sacred grass.
5 O ancient Herald, be glad in this rite and fellowship:
 Listen well to these songs.
6 Whatever we sacrifice perpetually to God and God,
 That gift is offered to you.
7 May he be our dear household lord, priest, pleasant and choice-worthy,
 May we, with bright fires, be dear to him.
8 The gods, honored by brilliant fires, have bestowed precious wealth on us,
 So, with bright fires, we pray to you.
9 And, O Immortal One, may the praises of mortals belong to us and you alike.
10 With all your fires, O Agni, take pleasure in this sacrifice,
 And this speech, O Son of Strength.

HYMN XXVII. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01027.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 With reverence, I honor you, Agni, like a swift horse,
Imperial Lord of sacred rituals.
2 May the far-sighted One of Might, bringer of great happiness,
Who showers his gifts like rain, be with us.
3 Lord of all life, from near and far, protect us from the wicked man,
O Agni, evermore.
4 O Agni, graciously accept this offering to the gods,
And this new song of praise.
5 Grant us the highest strength, the strength beneath, and the strength between.
6 You give gifts, radiant One; near, like the waves of the Indus, you swiftly reach the worshipper.
7 The man who protects in battle, Agni, or urges to combat,
Is lord of endless strength.
8 No one may defeat him, mighty One: indeed, his glorious power is unmatched.
9 May he who lives among all people lead us through battle on war steeds,
And with the singers win the spoils.
10 Help, you who know praises, this work, this hymn to Rudra, the adorable one in every home.
11 May this our deity, great and boundless, smoke-bannered and brilliantly bright,
Urge us to strength and holy thought.
12 Like some rich lord of men, may he, Agni, the banner of the gods,
Be heard by us through our praises.
13 Glory to the gods, both mighty and lesser, both young and old!
If we have power, let us offer worship to the god: no better prayer than this, oh gods, acknowledge.

HYMN XXVIII. Indra, Etc.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01028.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 WHERE the broad base stone stands tall to squeeze the juice,
 O Indra, drink with thirsty heart the drops that mortar spits.
2 WHERE, like wide hips, the pressing plates are placed,
 O Indra, drink with thirsty heart the drops that mortar spits.
3 WHERE the woman marks and leans the pestle’s steady rise and fall,
 O Indra, drink with thirsty heart the drops that mortar spits.
4 WHERE, like reins guiding a horse, they tie the churn’s staff with ropes,
 O Indra, drink with thirsty heart the drops that mortar spits.
5 IF indeed in every home you stand for work, Mortar,
 Here let your purest sound ring out, loud as conquerors’ drums.
6 O Sovereign of the Forest, as the breeze softly blows before you,
 Mortar, for Indra press forth Soma juice that he may drink.
7 BEST strength-givers, you spread wide your jaws, O Sacrificial Tools,
 Like two stallions chomping grass.
8 YOU Sovereigns of the Forest, both swift, with swift presses today
 Press sweet Soma juice for Indra’s drink.
9 TAKE up in cups what remains: the Soma on the filter pour,
 And on the ox-hide set the dregs.

HYMN XXIX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01029.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O Soma drinker, ever true, though hopeless we may be,
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

2 O Strength’s lord, whose jaws are strong, great deeds you do, mighty one:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

3 Let those who gaze upon each other fall asleep, never to wake again:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

4 Make all enemies sleep, and make gentle spirits wake:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

5 Crush this donkey, Indra, that brays dissonantly to you:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

6 Let the storm fall far in forests, circling in its course:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

7 Slay each slanderer, and destroy the one who secretly harms us:
 Do thou, O Indra, grant us hope of beautiful horses and cattle,
 In thousands, O richest one.

HYMN XXX. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01030.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 We seek strength with Soma drops, fill full your Indra like a well,
Most liberal, Lord of Hundred Powers,
2 Who lets a hundred of the pure, a thousand of the milk-blent draughts
Flow, even as down a depth, to him;
3 When for the strong, the rapturous joy he makes room within his belly,
Like the sea.
4 This is yours. You draw near, as a pigeon to its mate:
You care for this our prayer.
5 O Hero, Lord of Bounties, praised in hymns, may power and joyfulness
Be his who sings the laud to you.
6 Lord of a Hundred Powers, stand up to lend us succour in this fight
In others too let us agree.
7 In every need, in every fray we call as friends to succour us
Indra the mightiest of all.
8 If he will hear us let him come with succour of a thousand kinds,
And all that strengthens, to our call.
9 I call him mighty to resist, the Hero of our ancient home,
Thee whom my sire invoked of old.
10 We pray to thee, O much-invoked, rich in all precious gifts, O Friend,
Kind God to those who sing thy praise.
11 O Soma-drinker, Thunder-armed, Friend of our lovely-featured dames
And of our Soma-drinking friends.
12 Thus, Soma-drinker, may it be; thus, Friend, who wieldeth thunder, act
To aid each wish as we desire.
13 With Indra splendid feasts be ours, rich in all strengthening things wherewith,
Wealthy in food, we may rejoice.
14 Like thee, thyself, the singers' Friend, thou movest, as it were, besought,
Bold One, the axle of the car.
15 That, Śatakratu, thou to grace and please thy praisers, as it were,
Stirrst the axle with thy strength.
16 With champing, neighing loudly-snorting horses Indra hath ever won himself great treasures
A car of gold hath he whose deeds are wondrous received from us, and let us too receive it.
17 Come, Aśvins, with enduring strength wealthy in horses and in kine,
And gold, O ye of wondrous deeds.
18 Your chariot yoked for both alike, immortal, ye of mighty acts,

HYMN XXXI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01031.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Agni, thou wast the earliest Aṅgiras, a Seer; thou wast, a God thyself, the Gods’ auspicious Friend.
After thy holy ordinance, the Maruts, sage and active through wisdom, with their glittering spears, were born.
2 O Agni, thou, the best and earliest Aṅgiras, fulfill as a Sage the holy law of Gods.
Sprung from two mothers, wise, through all existence spread, resting in many a place for sake of living man.
3 First thou, Agni, wast disclosed to Mātariśvan, and to Vivasvān through thy noble inward power.
Heaven and Earth, Vasu! Shook at the choosing of the Priest: the burden thou didst bear, worshipped mighty Gods.
4 Agni thou madest heaven to thunder for mankind; thou, more pious, for pious Purūravas.
When thou art rapidly freed from thy parents, first eastward they bear thee round, and, after, to the west.
5 Thou, Agni, art a Bull who makes our store increase, to be invoked by him who lifts the ladle up.
Well knowing the oblation with the hallowing word, uniting all who live, thou lightenest first our folk.
6 Agni, thou savest in the synod when pursued even him, farseeing One! who walks in evil ways.
Thou, when the heroes fight for spoil which men rush, round, slayest in war the many by the hands of few.
7 For glory, Agni, day by day, thou liftest up the mortal man to highest immortality,
Even thou who yearning for both races give them great bliss, and to the prince grantest abundant food.
8 O Agni, highly lauded, make our singer famous that he may win us store of riches:
May we improve the rite with new performance. O Earth and Heaven, with all the Gods, protect us.
9 Agni, you lie in thy Parents' lap, a God among the Gods, be watchful for our good.
Former of bodies, be the singer's Providence: all good things hast thou sown for him, auspicious One!
10 Agni, thou art our Providence, our Father thou: we are thy brethren and thou art our spring of life.
In thee, rich in good heroes, guard of high decrees, meet hundred, thousand treasures, O inf


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XXXII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01032.htm
--------------------------------------------------
I will declare the manly deeds of Indra, the first to achieve them, the Thunder-wielder.

He slew the Dragon, then revealed the waters, and split the mountain torrents' channels.

He slew the Dragon lying on the mountain: Tvaṣṭar fashioned his heavenly bolt of thunder.
Like swift-moving cows descending in a stream, the waters flowed down to the ocean.

Impetuous as a bull, he chose Soma and drank its juices in three sacred beakers.
Maghavan grasped the thunder as his weapon and struck down this firstborn of the Dragons.

When you, Indra, slew the Dragon's firstborn and overcame the enchanters' spells,
Then you gave life to Sun and Dawn and Heaven, and no foe stood against you.

With your great and deadly thunder, Indra smote Vṛtra, the worst of Vṛtras.
As trunks of trees fall when the axe strikes them, so lies the prostrate Dragon on the ground.

Like a mad, weak warrior, Vṛtra challenged Indra, the mighty, many-slaying Hero.
Brooking not the clash of weapons, he crushed Indra's foes, the shattered forts falling.

Still unfooted and handless, Vṛtra challenged Indra, who struck him between the shoulders.
Emasculated yet claiming manly vigor, Vṛtra lay with his limbs scattered.

There, like a bursting river, he lies, the waters taking courage to flow above him.
The Dragon lies beneath the feet of torrents that Vṛtra had encompassed.

Then Vṛtra's mother was humbled; Indra cast his deadly bolt against her.
Above her was the mother, below was the son, and like a cow beside her calf lay Danu.

Rolled in ceaseless currents, the waters bear off Vṛtra's nameless body.
The foe of Indra sank into darkness, and Vṛtra's nameless body is borne away.

Guarded by Ahi stood the thralls of Dāsas, the waters stayed like kine held by the robber.
But when he smote Vṛtra, he opened the cave where the floods had been imprisoned.

Thy tail was like a horse's when thou, O Indra, struck on thy bolt; thou, God without a second,
Thou hast won back the kine, hast won the Soma; thou hast let loose to flow the Seven Rivers.

Nothing availed him lightning, nothing thunder, hailstorm or

HYMN XXXIII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01033.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Come, let us seek glory to Indra: he will guide us with greater care.
Will he not grant us perfect knowledge of this wealth, of cattle?
2 I fly to him, the Wealth-giver, invisible, as a falcon flies to its cherished nest,
With finest hymns of praise, honoring Indra, whom they invoke in battle.
3 Among his hosts, he ties the bowstring; he drives cattle from whatever foe pleases:
Gathering great stores of riches, Indra, do not trade with us, most mighty one.
4 You slew the wealthy Dasyu, alone but with your helpers, Indra!
Far from the floor of heaven, the ancient riteless ones fled to destruction.
5 Fighting with pious worshippers, the riteless turned and fled, Indra! with faces averted.
When you, fierce Lord of the Bay Steeds, the Stayer, blew from earth and sky the godless.
6 They met in battle the army of the blameless; then the Navagvas exerted all their power.
Like castrated men contending with men, they fled, conscious, by steep paths from Indra, scattered.
7 Whether they weep or laugh, you have overthrown them, O Indra, at the sky’s extreme limit.
The Dasyu you burned from heaven, and welcomed the prayer of him who offers Soma and praises you.
8 Adorned with their array of gold and jewels, they cover the earth with a covering veil.
Although they hastened, they did not overcome Indra: his spies he surrounds with the Sun of dawn.
9 As you enjoy heaven and earth, O Indra, surrounded by your greatness on every side,
So you with priests have blown away the Dasyu, and those who worship with those who worship.
10 Those who crossed the earth’s utmost limit did not subdue the Wealth-bestower with their charms:
Indra, the Bull, made his ally the thunder, and with its light milked cows from darkness.
11 The waters flowed according to their nature; he raided the navigable streams, grew mighty.
Then Indra, with his spirit concentrated, struck him forever with his strongest weapon.
12 Indra broke through Ilībiśa’s strong castles, and Śuṣṇa with his horn he cut to pieces:
You, Maghavan, for all his might and swiftness, slew your fighting foe with your thunder.
13

HYMN XXXIV. Aśvins.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01034.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Ye who observe this day be with us even thrice: your bounty stretches far, Aśvins and your course.
 To you, as to a cloak in winter, we cling close: you are to be drawn nigh by the wise.
 2 In your honey-car, three are the felloes that follow Soma’s dear one, as all know.
 Three pillars set beneath it for support: three times you journey by night, O Aśvins, three times by day.
 3 Three times in the same day, you Gods who banish want, sprinkle thrice today our sacrifice with mead;
 And three times grant us store of food with plenteous strength, at evening, O you Aśvins, and at break of day.
 4 Three times come to our home, three times to the righteous folk, three times aid the man who well deserves your help.
 Three, O you Aśvins, give us what shall make us glad; three times send us store of food as nevermore to fail.
 5 Three, O you Aśvins, bring to us abundant wealth; three times in the assembly of the Gods, three times assist our thoughts.
 Three, grant us prosperity, three grant us fame; for the Sun’s daughter has mounted your three-wheeled chariot.
 6 Three times, Aśvins, grant us the heavenly medicines, three times those of earth and three times those held by the waters,
 Bestow favour and health and strength upon my son; triple protection, Lords of Splendour, grant to him.
 7 Three times each day we worship you, O Aśvins; three, O you Aśvins, you travel around the earth.
 Car-borne from afar, O Nāsatyas, come, like vital air to bodies, come to the three.
 8 Three, O you Aśvins, with the Seven Mother Streams; three are the jars, the triple offering is prepared.
 Three are the worlds, and moving on above the sky you guard the firm-set vault of heaven through days and nights.
 9 Where are the three wheels of your triple chariot, where are the three seats firmly fastened?
 When will you yoke the mighty ass that draws it, to bring you to our sacrifice, Nāsatyas?
 10 Nāsatyas, come: the sacred gift is offered up; drink the sweet juice with lips that know the sweetness well.
 Savitar

HYMN XXXV. Savitar.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01035.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Agni, I invoke for our prosperity; I call on Mitra and Varuṇa to aid us here.
I call on Night that gives rest to all living things; I call on Savitar, the God, to lend us help.

Throughout the dusky sky advancing, laying to rest the immortal and the mortal,
Borne in his golden chariot he comes, Savitar, the God who looks on every creature.

The God moves by the upward path, the downward; with two bright Bays, adorable, he journeys.
Savitar comes, the God from afar, chasing from us all distress and sorrow.

His chariot adorned with pearls, of various colors, lofty, with golden pole, the God mounts,
The many-rayed One, Savitar the holy, bound, bearing power and might, for darksome regions.

With white hooves, the God manifests light to all the peoples; held in Savitar’s lap, divine One, all men, all beings have their place forever.

There are three heavens; two Savitar’s, adjacent: in Yama’s world is one, the home of heroes.
As on a linch-pin, firm, things immortal rest; he who knows it, let him declare it.

Strong-winged, he has lightened up the regions, deep-quivering Asura, the gentle Leader.
Now where is Sūrya? Where is one to tell us which celestial sphere his ray has wandered?

The earth’s eight points his brightness illuminates, three desert regions, and the Seven Rivers.
God Savitar, the gold-eyed, has come here, bestowing choice treasures on him who worships.

Golden-handed Savitar, far-seeing, travels between the earth and heaven,
Driving away sickness, bidding the Sun approach us, spreading the bright sky through the darksome region.

May he, gold-handed Asura, kind Leader, come to us with his help and favor.
Driving off Rākṣasas and Yātudhānas, the God is present, praised in hymns at evening.

O Savitar, your ancient dustless pathways are well established in the air’s mid-region:
O God, come by those fair paths to travel, preserve us from harm today, and bless us.

HYMN XXXVI. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01036.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 With words sent forth in holy hymns, Agni we invoke, the Lord
 Of many families who duly serve the Gods, yes, him whom others also praise.
 2 Men have won Agni, him who makes their strength abundant: we, with offerings, worship thee.
 Our gracious Helper in our deeds of might, be thou, O Excellent, this day.
 3 We choose thee for our messenger, thee, the Omniscient, for our Priest.
 The flames of thee the mighty are spread wide around: thy brilliance reaches to the sky.
 4 The Gods enkindle thee their ancient messenger—Varuṇa, Mitra, Aryaman.
 That mortal man, O Agni, gains through thee all wealth, who offers sacrifices to thee.
 5 Thou, Agni, art a cheering Priest, Lord of the House, men’s messenger:
 All constant high decrees established by the Gods, gathered together, meet in thee.
 6 In thee, the auspicious One, O Agni, youthfullest, each sacred gift is offered up:
 This day, and after, gracious, worship thou our Gods, that we may have heroic sons.
 7 To him in his own splendor draw near in worship the devout.
 Men ignite Agni with their sacrificial gifts, victorious over enemies.
 8 They struck down Vṛtra and slew it, made the earth and heaven and firmament a wide abode.
 The glorious Bull, invoked, stood at Kaṇva’s side: loud neighed the Steed for kine.
 9 Sit here, for thou art mighty; shine, best entertainer of the Gods.
 Worthy of sacred food, praised Agni! Loose the smoke, ruddy and beautiful to see.
 10 Bearer of offerings, whom, best sacrificing Priest, the Gods for Manu’s sake ordained;
 Whom Kaṇva, whom Medhyātithi made the source of wealth, and Vṛṣan and Upastuta.
 11 Him, Agni, whom Medhyātithi, whom Kaṇva kindled for his rite,
 Him these our songs of praise, him, Agni, we extol: his powers shine out preeminent.
 12 Make our wealth perfect thou, O Agni, Lord divine: for thou hast kinship with the Gods.
 Thou rulest as a King over widely-famous strength: be good to us, for thou art great.

HYMN XXXVII. Maruts.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01037.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Sing forth, O Kaṇvas, to your band of Maruts unassailable,
Playing, radiant on their chariot.

2 Those who, self-luminous, were born together, with the spotted deer,
Spears, swords, and glittering ornaments.

3 One hears, as though it were close at hand, the cracking of the whips they hold
They gather glory on their way.

4 Now sing the God-given hymn to your exultant Marut host,
The fiercely-vigorous, the strong.

5 Praise the Bull among the cows; for it is the Maruts' sportive band:
It strengthened as it drank the rain.

6 Who is your mightiest, Heroes, when, O shakers of the earth and heaven,
You shake them like a garment's hem?

7 At your approach, man holds him down before the fury of your wrath:
The rugged-jointed mountain yields.

8 They at whose races forth the earth, like an aged lord of men,
Trembles in terror on their ways.

9 Strong is their birth: vigour have they to issue from their Mother; strength,
Yea, even twice enough, is theirs.

10 And these, the Sons, the Singers, in their races have enlarged the bounds,
So that the kine must walk knee-deep.

11 Before them, on the ways they go, they drop this offspring of the cloud,
Long, broad, and inexhaustible.

12 O Maruts, as your strength is great, so have ye cast men down on earth,
So have ye made the mountains fall.

13 While the Maruts pass along, they talk together on the way:
Doth any hear them as they speak?

14 Come quickly with swift steeds, for ye have worshippers among Kaṇva's sons
May you rejoice among them well.

15 All is prepared for your delight. We are their servants evermore,
To live as long as life may last.

HYMN XXXVIII. Maruts.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01038.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 What now? When will you hold us close, like a father his child,
O gods, for whom sacred grass is cut?
2 Now where to? To which of your goals in heaven do you go,
And not on earth, where your cows play?
3 Where do your latest favors show? Where, Maruts, your prosperity?
Where all your high joys reside?
4 If, O Maruts, you the sons born by Prśni were mortal, and
The immortal one who praises you.
5 Then never would I be loathed like a wild beast in the field,
Nor should I go on Yama’s path.
6 Let not pestilence strike us with each new plague, hard to defeat,
Let each leave us, with drought alone.
7 Truly, Rudra’s fierce and mighty Sons send their unclouded rain
Even to desolate lands.
8 Like a cow the lightning bleats and follows, motherly, her calf,
When their rain-swollen flood is released.
9 When they flood the earth, they spread darkness even in daylight,
With the water-drenched rain-cloud.
10 O Maruts, at your voice’s sound, this earthly home shakes,
And each man reels who lives within.
11 O Maruts, with your swift hooves, unhindered in your paths,
Hasten along the bright embankments.
12 May your wheels be firm and steady, may your horses and chariots be
Steady, and may your reins be well-made.
13 Invite this song, for praise, Agni, Lord of Prayer,
Who is fair as Mitra is.
14 Form the hymn of praise in your mouth, make it like a rainy cloud,
Sing forth the measured eulogy.
15 Glory to the Marut host, worthy, tuneful, vigorous:
Here may the Strong Ones dwell with us.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XXXIX Maruts.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01039.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 When, like flames, from afar, Maruts, you cast your measure, where do you go, who shake the earth, moved by your wisdom and design?

2 Make your weapons strong to drive off your enemies, make them firm for defense, not as a cunning mortal.

3 When what is strong you overthrow, and turn everything heavy, heroes, your path through the forest trees and rock crevices.

4 You devour your foes, no enemy of yours exists in heaven or on earth: Rudras, may the strength held in this bond be yours, to defy now.

5 You make mountains tremble, you tear apart the forest kings, onward, Maruts, drive like drunken creatures, gods with your whole company.

6 You yoke the spotted deer to your chariot, a red deer leads, the Earth herself listens as you approach, and men are terribly afraid.

7 O Rudras, we urgently seek your aid for this work. Come to us with your help as in olden days, now for Kaṇva’s sake.

8 If any monstrous foe, O Maruts, sent by you or mortals threaten us, tear him from us with your power and might, and with the help that is yours.

9 For you, the worshipful and wise, have protected Kaṇva perfectly. O Maruts, come to us with full protection, like lightning seeks the rain.

10 All your strength, O Bountiful Ones, perfect, shaking the earth, Maruts, send an enemy like a dart against the poet’s wrathful foe.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XL. Brahmaṇaspati
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01040.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 O BRAHMANASPATHI, stand up: May God-serving men we pray to thee.
May those who give good gifts, the MARUTS, come to us. Indra, most swift, be thou with them.
2 O Son of Strength, each mortal calls to thee for aid when spoil of battle waits for him.
O MARUTS, may this man who loves you well obtain wealth of good steeds and hero might.
3 May BRAHMANASPATHI draw nigh, may SUNURTA the Goddess come,
And Gods bring to this rite which gives the five-fold gift the Hero, lover of mankind.
4 He who bestows a noble reward on the priest wins fame that never shall decay.
For him we offer sacred hero-giving food, peerless and conquering easily.
5 Now BRAHMANASPATHI speaks forth aloud the solemn hymn of praise,
Wherein INDRA and VARUṆA, MITRA, ARYAMAN, the Gods, have made their dwelling place.
6 May we in holy synods, Gods! recite that hymn, peerless, that brings felicity.
If you, O Heroes, graciously accept this word, may it obtain all bliss from you.
7 Who shall approach the pious? Who the man whose sacred grass is trimmed?
The offerer with his folk advances more and more: he fills his house with precious things.
8 He amplifies his lordly might, with kings he slays: even in battles, great or small,
None checks him, none subdues—wielder of the thunderbolt.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLI. Varuṇa, Mitra, Aryaman.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01041.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 NE’ER is he injured whom the Gods Varuṇa, Mitra, Aryaman,
The wisely wise, protect.
2 He prospers ever, free from harm, whom they, with full hands, enrich,
Whom they preserve from every foe.
3 The Kings drive far away his troubles and his enemies,
And lead him safely over distress.
4 Thornless, Ādityas, is the path, easy for him who seeks the Law:
With him there’s nothing to anger you.
5 What sacrifice, Ādityas, do you Heroes guide by the path direct—
May that come near to your thought.
6 That mortal, ever unyielding, gains wealth and every precious thing,
And children also of his own.
7 How, my friends, shall we prepare Aryaman’s and Mitra’s praise,
Glorious food of Varuṇa?
8 I point not out to you a man who strikes the pious, or reviles:
Only with hymns I call you near.
9 Let him not love to speak ill words: but fear the One who holds all four
Within his hand, until they fall.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLII. Pūṣan.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01042.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Shorten our paths, O Pūṣan, drive away obstacles on our journey:
Come near before us, cloud-born God.
2 Drive, Pūṣan, the wolf from our path, the wicked one who lurks to harm us,
Who waits in ambush to do us wrong.
3 He who lurks along our way, the thief with a deceitful heart:
Drive him far from our path.
4 With your foot, crush out the firebrand of the wicked one,
The double-tongued, whoever they may be.
5 Wise Pūṣan, Wonder-Worker, grant us now the aid you gave to our ancestors,
To help them prosper long ago.
6 As Lord of all prosperity, best wielder of the golden sword,
Make it easy to win riches.
7 Lead us past all pursuers, make our path pleasant and fair to walk:
O Pūṣan, grant us power for this.
8 Lead us to lush meadows filled with grass: send no early heat on our way:
O Pūṣan, grant us power for this.
9 Be kind to us, fill us with strength, feed us, and invigorate:
O Pūṣan, grant us power for this.
10 We have no fault to find with Pūṣan; we sing his praises with song:
We seek the Mighty One for wealth.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLIII. Rudra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01043.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 What shall we sing to Rudra, powerful, most generous, supremely wise,
That he might hold it dear?
2 That Aditi might grant Rudra's favor to our people, our cattle,
Our herds and offspring;
3 That Mitra and Varuṇa, and Rudra might remember us,
All gods together in accord.
4 To Rudra, Lord of sacrifice, of hymns and balmy remedies,
We pray for joy, health, and strength.
5 He shines with radiance like the Sun, as golden as bright gold,
The good, the best among the gods.
6 May he grant health to our horses, well-being to our rams and ewes,
To men, to women, and to cattle.
7 O Soma, let you bestow upon us the glory of a hundred men,
The great fame of mighty chiefs.
8 Let no malice, nor those who trouble Soma, hinder us.
Indu, give us a share of strength.
9 Soma! take hold, center, love these; Soma! know them as serving you,
Children of you Immortal, at the highest place of holy law.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLIV. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01044.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 IMMORTAL Jātavedas, you radiant offering-bearer, today bring the Gods to him who offers sacrifices.
2 You are the messenger and beloved messenger, the charioteer of sacrifice:
Grant us heroic strength and lofty fame, O Aśvins and Dawn.
3 We choose you, Agni, the good one whom many love,
Smoke-bannered, spreading light at the break of day, at sacrificial rites.
4 Noblest and most youthful, dear to those who offer gifts,
Gentle Agni, Jātavedas, I pray you bring the Gods to us at dawn.
5 I will glorify you, Agni, immortal sustainer of the world,
Deathless offering-bearer, fit for sacred food, preserver, best at sacrifice.
6 Tell your praiser good things, O most youthful God, richly worshipped, honey-tongued,
And, granting Praskaṇva long life, honor the Heavenly Host.
7 Agni, kindle us as possessor and Priest, all invoked,
So Agni, much-invoked, bring the Gods with all speed to us.
8 At dawn and night, Uṣas and Savitar, the Aśvins, Bhaga, Agni himself:
Skilled in fair rites, with Soma poured, light thee, oblation-waving God.
9 Agni, Lord of sacrifice and messenger of men, bring the Gods who wake at dawn, who see the light, to drink the Soma juice.
10 You shine forth, Agni, after former dawns, all visible, rich in light.
You are our help in battle, the Friend of man, great high priest in sacrifice.
11 Like Manu, we will establish you, Agni, performer of the rite,
Invoker, ministering Priest, wise and swift, immortal messenger.
12 As the Gods' High Priest, beloved by many, you fulfill their mission as their closest friend,
Then, like the far-reaching waves of the flood, let your flames roar aloud.
13 Hear, Agni, with ears to hear, all your divine retinue;
Let Mitra, Aryaman, seek our rite, seat them on the sacred grass.
14 Let those who support Law, generous givers, life-tongued Maruts, hear our praise.
May Law-supporting Varuṇa, with the Aśvins, drink the Soma juice.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLV. Agni.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01045.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Worship the Vasus, Agni! Here, the Rudras, the Ādityas, all
 Those born from Manu, those who know fair rites, who pour their blessings down.
 2 Agni, the Gods who understand give ear to the worshipper:
 Lord of Red Steeds, who loves song, bring those Three-and-Thirty Gods.
 3 O Jātavedas, great in action, listen to Praskaṇva's call,
 As Priyamedha did before, Atri, Virūpa, Aṅgiras.
 4 The sons of Priyamedha skilled in lofty praise have called for help
 On Agni who with radiant flame is Ruler of all holy rites.
 5 Hear these praises, invoked with holy oil, generous giver of rewards,
 By the sons of Kaṇva to call thee to their aid.
 6 O Agni, beloved by many, you of most wondrous fame, in their homes
 Men call on you whose hair is flame, to bear their offerings.
 7 Agni, best to find wealth, widely known, quick to hear,
 Singers have established in rites Herald and priestly assistant.
 8 Singers with Soma pressed have made you, Agni, hasten to the feast,
 Great light to mortal worshipper, when they bring the sacred gift.
 9 Good, bountiful, Son of Strength, today seat the Gods here on sacred grass
 Who come at dawn, the heavenly host, to drink the Soma juice.
 10 Bring with joint invocations, O Agni, the celestial host:
 Here stands the Soma, bountiful Gods drink this expressed yesterday.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLVI. Aśvins.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01046.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Now Morning, with her first light, shines bright, dear daughter of the sky:
High, Aśvins, I praise your worth,
2 Sons of the sea, mighty to save, discoverers of treasure, you
Gods with deep thought who find wealth.

3 Your giant horses race across the fiery land,
When your chariot flies with swift steeds.

4 You are generous, lover of the flood, Lord of the house, vigilant,
Feeding chiefs with offerings.

5 You listen to our hymns, Nāsatyas, thinking of our words:
Drink freely of the Soma juice.

6 Grant us, O Aśvin pair, such strength that, with attendant light,
May lead us through the darkness.

7 Come in the ship of our hymns to the far shore, O Aśvins,
Harness your chariot.

8 The wide vessel of the heavens is yours, on the flood's shore your chariot waits,
Drops, with the hymn, have been prepared.

9 Kaṇvas, the drops are in the sky; the wealth is at the waters' edge:
Where will you manifest your form?

10 Light came to lighten up the branch, the Sun appeared like gold:
And with its tongue it shone the dark.

11 The path of sacrifice was made to reach the distant goal:
The road of heaven was manifest.

12 The singer of their praise awaits whatever grace the Aśvins give,
Who save when Soma makes them glad.

13 You dwellers with Vivasvān come, auspicious, as to Manu before:
Come to the Soma and our praise.

14 O circumpolar Aśvins, Dawn follows the brightness of your path:
Approve with beams our solemn rites.

15 Drink of our libations, grant protection, O Aśvins two,
With aids that none can break.

HYMN XLVII. Aśvins.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01047.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Aśvins, for you this sweet Soma has been poured; drink it now, offered yesterday, and grant wealth to the giver.
 2 Come, Aśvins, on your three-wheeled chariot, beautiful in form, at the sacrifice the Kaṇvas pray to you.
 3 O Aśvins, who uphold Law, drink this Soma; on the car laden with wealth come to him who offers it.
 4 Wise Aśvins, sprinkle the sacrifice with the sweet juice on the triple heaped grass.
 The sons of Kaṇva, striving to reach heaven, call on you with Soma poured out.
 5 O Aśvins, with those protections with which you guarded Kaṇva, keep us, Lords of Splendor; drink the Soma, strengtheners of holy Law.
 6 O Mighty Ones, you gave Sudās abundant food, brought your treasure-laden car;
 Now grant us wealth, much desired, from heaven or the sea.
 7 Nāsatyas, whether far or near, in Turvaśa, come on your lightly rolling chariot, with the sunbeams.
 8 Let your chariots, adorned for sacrifice, bring you to our libations; bestow food on the giver and the giver-rightly.
 9 Chiefs, sit on the sacred grass, on your chariot decked with a sunbright canopy, where you always bring wealth to the worshipper.
 10 With praises and songs of praise we call you down, rich ones, to help us; for you have always in the Kaṇvas' beloved house drunk the Soma juice.

HYMN XLVIII. Dawn.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01048.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 Dawn upon us with prosperity, O Uṣas, Daughter of the Sky,
Dawn with great glory, Goddess, Lady of the Light, bring us riches, Abundant One.
2 They, bringing horses and cattle, givers of all wealth, often come to lighten us.
O Uṣas, wake up for me the sounds of joy: send us the riches of the great.
3 Uṣas has dawned, and now shall dawn, the Goddess, driver forth of chariots
Which, as she approaches, fix their thoughts on her, like seekers on the flood.
4 Here, Kaṇva, chief of Kaṇva’s race, sings forth the glories of heroes’ names—
The princes, O Uṣas, as you approach, direct their thoughts to generous gifts.
5 Like a good matron Uṣas comes carefully tending everything:
Awakening all life, she stirs all creatures that walk, and makes the birds of air fly up.
6 She sends the busy forth, each man to his pursuit: delay she knows not as she springs.
O Rich in opulence, after your dawning birds that have flown no longer rest.
7 This Dawn has yoked her horses afar, beyond the rising Sun:
Borne on a hundred chariots, auspicious Dawn, advancing on her way to Men.
8 To meet her gaze all living creatures bend down: Excellent One, she makes the light.
Uṣas, Daughter of the Sky, rich in opulence, banishes foes and enemies.
9 Shine on us with your radiant light, O Uṣas, Daughter of the Sky,
Bringing to us great stores of high happiness, and beaming on our solemn rites.
10 For in you is the breath and life of every living creature, when, Excellent, you rise.
Borne on your lofty chariot, O Lady of the Light, hear, you of wondrous wealth, our call.
11 O Uṣas, gain yourself the strength that among men is wonderful.
Bring the pious to holy rites, those who as priests sing praise to you.
12 Bring from the heavens, O Uṣas, all the gods, so they may drink our Soma juice,
And, being what you are, grant us cattle and horses, strength fit for praise and hero might.
13 May Uṣas, whose auspicious rays shine around, grant us great riches, fair in form, of all good things, wealth that labor


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN XLIX. Dawn.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01049.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 From the sky’s bright realm, Uṣas, come in auspicious ways:
Let red steeds carry you to the house that pours the Soma, juice.

2 Mount your fair-shaped chariot, O Uṣas, swift to move,
With it, O Daughter of the Sky, help men of noble fame today.

3 Bright Uṣas, when your times return, all creatures stir,
And winged birds from all the boundaries of heaven gather around.

4 You, as you are, the Kaṇvas, seeking wealth, call out to you
With sacred songs, the radiant realm you light with your beams.

HYMN L. Sūrya.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01050.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 His bright rays carry him up high, the God who knows all living beings,
 Surya, that all may see him.
 2 The constellations pass away, like thieves, along with their beams,
 Before the all-seeing Sun.
 3 His radiant rays are seen far off, across the world of men,
 Like flames of fire that burn and blaze.
 4 Swift and all beautiful art thou, O Surya, maker of the light,
 Illuming all the radiant realm.
 5 You go to the company of gods, you come here to humans,
 Here to behold all light.
 6 With that same eye of yours by which you make Varuṇa brilliant,
 Upon the busy race of men,
 7 Traveling through the sky and wide air, you measure out our days,
 Sun, seeing all that comes into being.
 8 Seven swift horses pull your chariot, O you far-sighted One,
 God, Surya, with the radiant hair.
 9 Surya has yoked the pure, bright seven, the daughters of the chariot; with these,
 His own dear team, he goes forth.
 10 Looking at the higher light above the darkness, we have come
 To Surya, God among the gods, the best light.
 11 Rising today, O rich in friends, ascending to the higher heaven,
 Surya remove my heart's disease, take from me this yellow hue.
 12 To parrots and to starlings give my yellowness away,
 Or transfer it to Haritāla trees.
 13 With all his victorious might this Aditya has gone up high,
 Giving my enemy into my hands: let me not be my enemy's prey.


--------------------------------------------------
HYMN LI. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01051.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 MAKE glad with songs that Ram whom many men invoke, worthy of songs of praise, Indra, the sea of wealth;
 Sing praise to him the Sage, most liberal for our good.

2 As aids the skilful Ṛbhus yearned to Indra strong to save, who fills mid-air, encompassed round with might,
 Rushing in rapture; and o’er Śatakratu came the gladdening shout that urged him on to victory.

3 Thou hast disclosed the kine's stall for the Aṅgirases, and made a way for Atri by a hundred doors.
 On Vimada thou hast bestowed both food and wealth, making thy bolt dance in the sacrificer's fight.

4 Thou hast unclosed the prisons of the waters; thou hast in the mountain seized the treasure rich in gifts.
 When thou hadst slain with might the dragon Vṛtra, thou, Indra, didst raise the Sun in heaven for all to see.

5 With wondrous might thou blew away enchanter fiends, with celestial powers those who called on thee in jest.
 Thou, hero-hearted, hast broken down Pipru's forts, and helped Ṛjiśvan when the Dasyus were struck dead.

6 Thou savedst Kutsa when Śuṣṇa was smitten down; to Atithigva gavest Śambara for a prey.
 E’en mighty Arbuda thou troddest under foot: thou from of old wast born to strike the Dasyus dead.

7 All power and might is closely gathered up in thee; thy bounteous spirit joys in drinking Soma juice.
 Known is the thunderbolt that lies within thine arms: rend off therewith all manly prowess of our foe.

8 Discern thou well Āryas and Dasyus; punishing the lawless give them up to him whose grass is strewn.
 Be thou the sacrificer's strong encourager all these thy deeds are my delight at festivals.

9 Indra gives up the lawless to the pious man, destroying by the Strong Ones those who have no strength.
 Vamra when glorified destroyed the gathered piles of the still waxing great one who would reach the heaven.

10 The might which Uśanā hath formed for thee with might rends in its greatness and with strength both worlds apart.
 O Hero-souled, the steeds of Vāta, yoked by thought, have carried thee to fame

HYMN LII. Indra.
URL: https://sacred-texts.com/hin/rigveda/rv01052.htm
--------------------------------------------------
1 I GLORY IN THAT INDRA WHO FINDS THE LIGHT OF HEAVEN, WHO HAS A HUNDRED NATURED FRIENDS GOING WITH HIM.

With hymns may I turn to Indra for my aid—his chariot, like a strong horse, rushes to the call.

2 Like a mountain firmly placed, unshaken, he, thousandfold protector, grew mighty in strength,
When Indra, rejoicing in the draughts of Soma, forced the clouds, slaying Vṛtra, who held back the rains.

3 He holds even the rain-stayers, spread over dark clouds rooted in light, strengthened by the wise.
Indra with thought, with skillful activity, I call, generous giver, for he fills with the juice.

4 Those that flow in heaven on sacred grass, his own assistants, nobly-natured, fill like the sea—
Beside that Indra when he struck down Vṛtra, his helpers sped like swift streams down a slope,
When Indra, thunder-armed, made bold by Soma draughts, as Tṛta cleaves Vala's fences, cleft him through.

5 As in wild joy he fought with him who stayed the rain, his helpers sped like swift streams down a slope,
When Indra, thunder-armed, made bold by Soma draughts, as Tṛta cleaved Vala's fences, cleft him through.

6 Encompassed by splendor, your warrior might shone forth; the rain-obstructer lay in mid-air's lowest deep,
What time, O Indra, you cast your thunder down upon the jaws of Vṛtra, hard to restrain.

7 The hymns that magnify you, Indra, reach to you even as water-brooks flow down and fill the lake.
Tvaṣṭar gave yet more force to your appropriate strength, and forged your thunderbolt of overpowering might.

8 When, Indra, you struck down Vṛtra with your Bay Steeds, causing floods to flow for man,
You held in your arms the metal thunderbolt, and set the Sun in the heaven for all to see.

9 In fear they raised the lofty hymn of praise, giving and effectual, leading up to heaven,
When Indra's helpers fighting for the good of men, the Maruts, faithful to mankind, joyed in the light.

10 Then Heaven himself, the mighty, at that Dragon's roar re
